ns-0 ns-subject page-Gini_coefficient rootpage-Gini_coefficient skin-vector action-view">\t\t<div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Gini coefficient</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Decision_tree_learning#Gini_impurity" title="Decision tree learning">Gini impurity</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>, the <b>Gini coefficient</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/d\xca\x92/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">d\xca\x92</span><span title="/i\xcb\x90/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">i\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">JEE</span>-nee</i></a>; sometimes expressed as a <b>Gini ratio</b> (or a <a href="/wiki/Normalization_(statistics)" title="Normalization (statistics)">normalized</a> <b>Gini index</b>)) is a <a href="/wiki/Statistical_dispersion#Measures_of_statistical_dispersion" title="Statistical dispersion">measure of statistical dispersion</a> intended to represent the income or wealth distribution of a nation\'s residents, and is the most commonly used measurement of inequality. It was developed by the <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Corrado_Gini" title="Corrado Gini">Corrado Gini</a> and published in his 1912 paper <i>Variability and Mutability</i> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Variabilit\xc3\xa0 e mutabilit\xc3\xa0</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGini1912_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGini1912-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Gini coefficient measures the inequality among values of a <a href="/wiki/Frequency_distribution" title="Frequency distribution">frequency distribution</a> (for example, levels of <a href="/wiki/Income" title="Income">income</a>). A Gini coefficient of zero expresses perfect equality, where all values are the same (for example, where everyone has the same income). A Gini coefficient of 1 (or 100%) expresses maximal inequality among values (e.g., for a large number of people, where only one person has all the income or consumption, and all others have none, the Gini coefficient will be very nearly one).<sup id="cite_ref-US_Census_Bureau_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_Census_Bureau-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> However, a value greater than one may occur if some persons represent negative contribution to the total (for example, having negative income or wealth). For larger groups, values close to or above 1 are very unlikely in practice. Given the normalization of both the cumulative population and the cumulative share of income used to calculate the Gini coefficient, the measure is not overly sensitive to the specifics of the income distribution, but rather only on how incomes vary relative to the other members of a population. The exception to this is in the redistribution of income resulting in a minimum income for all people.  When the population is sorted, if their income distribution were to approximate a well-known function, then some representative values could be calculated.\n</p><p>The Gini coefficient was proposed by Gini as a measure of <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">inequality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Income_inequality_metrics" title="Income inequality metrics">income</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wealth_concentration" class="mw-redirect" title="Wealth concentration">wealth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> For <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD countries</a>, in the late 20th century, considering the effect of taxes and <a href="/wiki/Transfer_payments" class="mw-redirect" title="Transfer payments">transfer payments</a>, the income Gini coefficient ranged between 0.24 and 0.49, with <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> being the lowest and <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> the highest.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> African countries had the highest pre-tax Gini coefficients in 2008\xe2\x80\x932009, with South Africa the world\'s highest, variously estimated to be 0.63 to 0.7,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> although this figure drops to 0.52 after social assistance is taken into account, and drops again to 0.47 after taxation.<sup id="cite_ref-moneywebSA_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moneywebSA-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The global income Gini coefficient in 2005 has been estimated to be between 0.61 and 0.68 by various sources.<sup id="cite_ref-fao2009_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-undp10_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undp10-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are some issues in interpreting a Gini coefficient. The same value may result from many different distribution curves. The demographic structure should be taken into account. Countries with an aging population, or with a baby boom, experience an increasing pre-tax Gini coefficient even if real income distribution for working adults remains constant. Scholars have devised over a dozen variants of the Gini coefficient.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-blomq81_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blomq81-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label tocsection-16"><a href="#Features_of_Gini_coefficient"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Features of Gini coefficient</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Other_uses"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Other uses</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg/310px-Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg.png" width="310" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg/465px-Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg/620px-Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical representation of the Gini coefficient<br /><br />The graph shows that the Gini coefficient is equal to the area marked <i>A</i> divided by the sum of the areas marked <i>A</i> and <i>B</i>, that is, <span class="nowrap">Gini = <i>A</i> / (<i>A</i> + <i>B</i>)</span>. It is also equal to <span class="nowrap"> 2<i>A</i></span> and to <span class="nowrap"> 1 \xe2\x88\x92 2<i>B</i></span> due to the fact that <span class="nowrap"><i>A</i> + <i>B</i> = 0.5</span> (since the axes scale from 0 to 1).</div></div></div>\n<p>The Gini coefficient is a single number aimed at measuring how far a country\xe2\x80\x99s wealth distribution deviates from totally equal distribution of productivity. \n</p><p>The Gini coefficient is usually defined <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematically</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_curve" title="Lorenz curve">Lorenz curve</a>, which plots the proportion of the total income of the population (y axis) that is cumulatively earned by the bottom x% of the population (see diagram). The line at 45 degrees thus represents perfect equality of incomes. The Gini coefficient can then be thought of as the <a href="/wiki/Ratio" title="Ratio">ratio</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Area" title="Area">area</a> that lies between the line of equality and the <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_curve" title="Lorenz curve">Lorenz curve</a> (marked <i>A</i> in the diagram) over the total area under the line of equality (marked <i>A</i> and <i>B</i> in the diagram); i.e., <span class="nowrap">G = <i>A</i> / (<i>A</i> + <i>B</i>)</span>. It is also equal to <span class="nowrap"> 2<i>A</i></span> and to <span class="nowrap"> 1 \xe2\x88\x92 2<i>B</i></span> due to the fact that <span class="nowrap"><i>A</i> + <i>B</i> = 0.5</span> (since the axes scale from 0 to 1).\n</p><p>If all people have non-negative income (or wealth, as the case may be), the Gini coefficient can theoretically range from 0 (complete equality) to 1 (complete inequality); it is sometimes expressed as a percentage ranging between 0 and 100. In practice, both extreme values are not quite reached. If negative values are possible (such as the negative wealth of people with debts), then the Gini coefficient could theoretically be more than 1. Normally the mean (or total) is assumed positive, which rules out a Gini coefficient less than zero.\n</p><p>An alternative approach is to define the Gini coefficient as half of the <a href="/wiki/Relative_mean_absolute_difference" class="mw-redirect" title="Relative mean absolute difference">relative mean absolute difference</a>, which is mathematically equivalent to the Lorenz curve definition.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\nThe mean absolute difference is the average <a href="/wiki/Absolute_difference" title="Absolute difference">absolute difference</a> of all pairs of items of the population, and the relative mean absolute difference is the mean absolute difference divided by the average, to normalize for scale. If <i>x<sub>i</sub></i> is the wealth or income of person <i>i</i>, and there are <i>n</i> persons, then the Gini coefficient <i>G</i> is given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle G={\\frac {\\displaystyle {\\sum _{i=1}^{n}\\sum _{j=1}^{n}\\left|x_{i}-x_{j}\\right|}}{\\displaystyle {2\\sum _{i=1}^{n}\\sum _{j=1}^{n}x_{j}}}}={\\frac {\\displaystyle {\\sum _{i=1}^{n}\\sum _{j=1}^{n}\\left|x_{i}-x_{j}\\right|}}{\\displaystyle {2n\\sum _{i=1}^{n}x_{i}}}}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>G</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <munderover>\n                  <mo>&#x2211;<!-- \xe2\x88\x91 --></mo>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                    <mi>i</mi>\n                    <mo>=</mo>\n                    <mn>1</mn>\n income (or wealth) distribution is given as a continuous <a href="/wiki/Probability_distribution_function" title="Probability distribution function">probability distribution function</a> <i>p(x)</i>, where <i>p(x)dx</i> is the fraction of the population with income <i>x</i> to <i>x+dx</i>, then the Gini coefficient is again half of the relative mean absolute difference:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span is the mean of the distribution <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mu =\\int _{-\\infty }^{\\infty }x\\,p(x)\\,dx}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>&#x03BC;<!-- \xce\xbc --></mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n            <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x221E;<!-- \xe2\x88\x9e --></mi>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x221E;<!-- \xe2\x88\x9e --></mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mi>x</mi>\n        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />\n        <mi>p</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <mi>x</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>x</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6221f8493d0b8d50d23bb1ce112368fa06e20589" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; positive.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Calculation">Calculation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Calculation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Example:_two_levels_of_income">Example: two levels of income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Example: two levels of income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg/220px-Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg/330px-Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg/440px-Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gini_coefficient_for_distribution_with_only_two_income_or_wealth_levels.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Richest <i>u</i>&#160;% of population (red) equally share <i>f</i>&#160;% of all income or wealth, others (green) equally share remainder: <span class="nowrap"><i>G</i> = <i>f</i> \xe2\x88\x92 <i>u</i></span>. A smooth distribution (blue) with same <i>u</i> and <i>f</i> always has <span class="nowrap"><i>G</i> &gt; <i>f</i> \xe2\x88\x92 <i>u</i></span>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The most equal society will be one in which every person receives the same income (<span class="nowrap"><i>G</i> = 0</span>); the most unequal society will be one in which a single person receives 100% of the total income and the remaining <span class="nowrap"><i>N</i> \xe2\x88\x92 1</span> people receive none (<span class="nowrap"><i>G</i> = 1 \xe2\x88\x92 1/<i>N</i></span>).\n</p><p>While the income distribution of any particular country need not follow simple functions, these functions give a qualitative understanding of the income distribution in a nation given the Gini coefficient.\n</p><p>An informative simplified case just distinguishes two levels of income, low and high. If the high income group is <i>u</i>&#160;% of the population and earns a fraction <i>f</i>&#160;% of all income, then the Gini coefficient is <span class="nowrap"><i>f</i> \xe2\x88\x92 <i>u</i></span>. An actual more graded distribution with these same values <i>u</i> and <i>f</i> will always have a higher Gini coefficient than <span class="nowrap"><i>f</i> \xe2\x88\x92 <i>u</i></span>.\n</p><p>The proverbial case where the richest 20% have 80% of all income (see <a href="/wiki/Pareto_principle" title="Pareto principle">Pareto principle</a>) would lead to an income Gini coefficient of at least 60%.\n</p><p>An often cited<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> case that 1% of all the world\'s population owns 50% of all wealth, means a wealth Gini coefficient of at least 49%.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternate_expressions">Alternate expressions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Alternate expressions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In some cases, this equation can be applied to calculate the Gini coefficient without direct reference to the Lorenz curve. For example, (taking <i>y</i> to mean the income or wealth of a person or household):\n</p>\n<ul><li>For a population uniform on the values <i>y</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>, <i>i</i> = 1 to <i>n</i>, indexed in non-decreasing order (<i>y</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> \xe2\x89\xa4 <i>y</i><sub><i>i</i>+1</sub>):</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline _{i=1}^{n}\\;(n+1-i)y_{i}}{\\sum \\limits _{i=1}^{n}y_{i}}}\\right)\\right)}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mo>(</mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mfrac>\n                  <mrow>\n                    <munderover>\n                      <mo movablelimits="false">&#x2211;<!-- \xe2\x88\x91 --></mo>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                        <mi>i</mi>\n                        <mo>=</mo>\n                        <mn>1</mn>\n                      </mrow>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                        <mi>n</mi>\n                      </mrow>\n                    </munderover>\n                    <mspace width="thickmathspace" />\n                    <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n                    <mi>n</mi>\n                    <mo>+</mo>\n                    <mn>1</mn>\n                    <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n                    <mi>i</mi>\n                    <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n                    <msub>\n                      <mi>y</mi>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                        <mi>i</mi>\n                      </mrow>\n                    </msub>\n                  </mrow>\n                  <mrow>\n                    <munderover>\n                      <mo movablelimits="false">&#x2211;<!-- \xe2\x88\x91 --></mo>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                       <mi>i</mi>\n                      </mrow>\n                    </msub>\n                  </mrow>\n                </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>)</mo>\n            </mrow>\n          </mrow>\n          <mo>)</mo>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle G={\\frac {1}{n}}\\left(n+1-2\\left({\\frac {\\sum \\limits _{i=1}^{n}\\;(n+1-i)y_{i}}{\\sum \\limits _{i=1}^{n}y_{i}}}\\right)\\right)}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/65484a887c9806c1d39d557041b4f595817ad2d5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -5.838ex; may be simplified to:</dd>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle G={\\frac {2\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}\\;iy_{i}}{n\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}y_{i}}}-{\\frac {n+1}{n}}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>G</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mn>2</mn>\n              <msubsup>\n                <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x03A3;<!-- \xce\xa3 --></mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>i</mi>\n                  <mo>=</mo>\n                  <mn>1</mn>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>n</mi>\n                </mrow>\n              </msubsup>\n              <mspace width="thickmathspace" />\n              <mi>i</mi>\n              <msub>\n                <mi>y</mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>i</mi>\n                </mrow>\n              </msub>\n            </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>n</mi>\n              <msubsup>\n                <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x03A3;<!-- \xce\xa3 --></mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>i</mi>\n                  <mo>=</mo>\n                  <mn>1</mn>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>n</mi>\n                </mrow>\n              </msubsup>\n              <msub>\n                <mi>y</mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>i</mi>\n                </mrow>\n              </msub>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>n</mi>\n              <mo>+</mo>\n              <mn>1</mn>\n            </mrow>\n            <mi>n</mi>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle G={\\frac {2\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}\\;iy_{i}}{n\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}y_{i}}}-{\\frac {n+1}{n}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/401e1c01c8d1985a6d2ecee4a8398938db4568b5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:23.963ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="G={\\frac {2\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}\\;iy_{i}}{n\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}y_{i}}}-{\\frac {n+1}{n}}"/></span></dd>\n<dd>This formula actually applies to any real population, since each person can be assigned his or her own <i>y</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolfram_Mathworld_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfram_Mathworld-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p>Since the Gini coefficient is half the relative mean absolute difference, it can also be calculated using formulas for the relative mean absolute difference. For a random sample <i>S</i> consisting of values <i>y</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>, <i>i</i> = 1 to <i>n</i>, that are indexed in non-decreasing order (<i>y</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> \xe2\x89\xa4 <i>y</i><sub><i>i</i>+1</sub>), the statistic:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle G(S)={\\frac {1}{n-1}}\\left(n+1-2\\left({\\frac {\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}\\;(n+1-i)y_{i}}{\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}y_{i}}}\\right)\\right)}">\n These formulae are also applicable in the limit as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle n\\rightarrow \\infty }">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>n</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- \xe2\x86\x92 --></mo>\n        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x221E;<!-- \xe2\x88\x9e --></mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle n\\rightarrow \\infty }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9702f04f2d0e5b887b99faeeffb0c4cfd8263eee" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.333ex; height:1.843ex;" alt="n\\rightarrow \\infty "/></span>.</dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continuous_probability_distribution">Continuous probability distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Continuous probability distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When the population is large, the income distribution may be represented by a continuous <a href="/wiki/Probability_density_function" title="Probability density function">probability density function</a> <i>f(x)</i> where <i>f(x) dx</i> is the fraction of the population with wealth or income in the interval <i>dx</i> about <i>x</i>.  If <i>F(x)</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Cumulative_distribution_function" title="Cumulative distribution function">cumulative distribution function</a> for <i>f(x)</i>, then the Lorenz curve <i>L(F)</i> may then be represented as a function parametric in <i>L(x)</i> and <i>F(x)</i> and the value of <i>B</i> can be found by <a href="/wiki/Integral" title="Integral">integration</a>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle B=\\int _{0}^{1}L(F)dF.}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>B</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- \xe2\x88\xab --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>0</mn>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mi>L</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>F</mi>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle B=\\int _{0}^{1}L(F)dF.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8aec6fc57be153f05b82745dff949f368d1c45b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:17.504ex; height:6.176ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle B=\\int _{0}^{1}L(F)dF.}"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The Gini coefficient can also be calculated directly from the <a href="/wiki/Cumulative_distribution_function" title="Cumulative distribution function">cumulative distribution function</a> of the distribution <i>F</i>(<i>y</i>). Defining \xce\xbc as the mean of the distribution, and specifying that  <i>F</i>(<i>y</i>) is zero for all negative values, the Gini coefficient is given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span <mi>y</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <msup>\n          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msup>\n        <mi>d</mi>\n        <mi>y</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mn>1</mn>\n            <mi>&#x03BC;<!-- \xce\xbc --></mi>\n (Note that this formula can be applied when there are negative values if the integration is taken from minus infinity to plus infinity.)\n</p><p>The Gini coefficient may be expressed in terms of the <a href="/wiki/Quantile_function" title="Quantile function">quantile function</a> <i>Q</i>(<i>F</i>) (inverse of the cumulative distribution function: Q(F(x))=x)\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span Gini index can be calculated explicitly. For example, if <i>y</i> follows a <a href="/wiki/Lognormal_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Lognormal distribution">lognormal distribution</a> with the standard deviation of logs equal to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma }">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- \xcf\x83 --></mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/59f59b7c3e6fdb1d0365a494b81fb9a696138c36" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; distribution</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {x^{\\alpha -1}(1-x)^{\\beta -1}}{B(\\alpha ,\\beta )}}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <msup>\n                <mi>x</mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- \xce\xb1 --></mi>\n                  <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n                  <mn>1</mn>\n                </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mo              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- \xce\xb2 --></mi>\n                  <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n                  <mn>1</mn>\n                </mrow>\n              </msup>\n            </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>B</mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- \xce\xb1 --></mi>\n              <mo>,</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- \xce\xb2 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\frac {x^{\\alpha -1}(1-x)^{\\beta -1}}{B(\\alpha ,\\beta )}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fd843d3b4f8107294d472539c3e683e0f179f55f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:15.967ex; height:6.676ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {x^{\\alpha -1}(1-x)^{\\beta -1}}{B(\\alpha ,\\beta )}}}"/></span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle \\left({\\frac {2}{\\alpha }}\\right){\\frac {B(\\alpha +\\beta ,\\alpha +\\beta )}{B(\\alpha ,\\alpha )B(\\beta ,\\beta )}}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mrow>\n          <mo>(</mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mfrac>\n              <mn>2</mn>\n              <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- \xce\xb1 --></mi>\n            </mfrac>\n          </mrow>\n          <mo>)</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>B</mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- \xce\xb1 --></mi>\n              <mo>+</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- \xce\xb2 --></mi>\n              <mo>,</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- \xce\xb1 --></mi>\n              <mo>+</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- \xce\xb2 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n            </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>B</mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- \xce\xb1 --></mi>\n              <mo>,</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- \xce\xb1 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n              <mi>B</mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- \xce\xb2 --></mi>\n              <mo>,</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- \xce\xb2 --></mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\left({\\frac {2}{\\alpha }}\\right){\\frac {B(\\alpha +\\beta ,\\alpha +\\beta )}{B(\\alpha ,\\alpha )B(\\beta ,\\beta )}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/88be3deb7b13b3ff6ab2af9ce56629fed6c5980f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:22.895ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle \\left({\\frac {2}{\\alpha }}\\right){\\frac {B(\\alpha +\\beta ,\\alpha +\\beta )}{B(\\alpha ,\\alpha )B(\\beta ,\\beta )}}}"/></span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_approaches">Other approaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other approaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sometimes the entire Lorenz curve is not known, and only values at certain intervals are given. In that case, the Gini coefficient can be approximated by using various techniques for <a href="/wiki/Interpolation" title="Interpolation">interpolating</a> the missing values of the Lorenz curve. If (<i>X</i><sub><i>k</i></sub>, <i>Y</i><sub><i>k</i></sub>) are the known points on the Lorenz curve, with the <i>X</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> indexed in increasing order (<i>X</i><sub><i>k</i> \xe2\x80\x93 1</sub> &lt; <i>X</i><sub><i>k</i></sub>), so that:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>X</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> is the cumulated proportion of the population variable, for <i>k</i> = 0,...,<i>n</i>, with <i>X</i><sub>0</sub> = 0, <i>X</i><sub><i>n</i></sub> = 1.</li>\n<li><i>Y</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> is the cumulated proportion of the income variable, for <i>k</i> = 0,...,<i>n</i>, with <i>Y</i><sub>0</sub> = 0, <i>Y</i><sub><i>n</i></sub> = 1.</li>\n<li><i>Y</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> should be indexed in non-decreasing order (<i>Y</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> &gt; <i>Y</i><sub><i>k</i> \xe2\x80\x93 1</sub>)</li></ul>\n<p>If the Lorenz curve is approximated on each interval as a line between consecutive points, then the area B can be approximated with <a href="/wiki/Trapezoidal_rule" title="Trapezoidal rule">trapezoids</a> and:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle G_{1}=1-\\sum _{k=1}^{n}(X_{k}-X_{k-1})(Y_{k}+Y_{k-1})}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>G</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mn>1</mn>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <munderover>\n          <mo>&#x2211;<!-- \xe2\x88\x91 --></mo>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n            <mo>=</mo>\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>n</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </munderover>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>X</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>X</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n            <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>Y</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>+</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>Y</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n            <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle G_{1}=1-\\sum _{k=1}^{n}(X_{k}-X_{k-1})(Y_{k}+Y_{k-1})}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/61f86e18337c8c5101b9cddc69dfcafe9e52b2d3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:37.742ex; height:6.843ex;" alt="G_{1}=1-\\sum _{k=1}^{n}(X_{k}-X_{k-1})(Y_{k}+Y_{k-1})"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>is the resulting approximation for G. More accurate results can be obtained using other methods to <a href="/wiki/Numerical_integration" title="Numerical integration">approximate the area</a> B, such as approximating the Lorenz curve with a <a href="/wiki/Simpson%27s_rule" title="Simpson&#39;s rule">quadratic function</a> across pairs of intervals, or building an appropriately smooth approximation to the underlying distribution function that matches the known data. If the population mean and boundary values for each interval are also known, these can also often be used to improve the accuracy of the approximation.\n</p><p>The Gini coefficient calculated from a sample is a statistic and its standard error, or confidence intervals for the population Gini coefficient, should be reported. These can be calculated using <a href="/wiki/Resampling_(statistics)#Bootstrap" title="Resampling (statistics)">bootstrap</a> techniques but those proposed have been mathematically complicated and computationally onerous even in an era of fast computers. Ogwang (2000) made the process more efficient by setting up a "trick regression model" in which respective income variables in the sample are ranked with the lowest income being allocated rank 1. The model then expresses the rank (dependent variable) as the sum of a constant <i>A</i> and a <a href="/wiki/Normal_distribution" title="Normal distribution">normal</a> error term whose variance is inversely proportional to <i>y</i><sub><i>k</i></sub>;\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle k=A+\\ N(0,s^{2}/y_{k})}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>k</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>A</mi>\n        <mo>+</mo>\n        <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>\n        <mi>N</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <mn>0</mn>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n        <msup>\n          <mi>s</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>y</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle k=A+\\ N(0,s^{2}/y_{k})}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c56b1af5476f3ace651234955d6776f293380143" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:21.078ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="k=A+\\ N(0,s^{2}/y_{k})"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Ogwang showed that <i>G</i> can be expressed as a function of the weighted least squares estimate of the constant <i>A</i> and that this can be used to speed up the calculation of the <a href="/wiki/Resampling_(statistics)#Jackknife" title="Resampling (statistics)">jackknife</a> estimate for the standard error. Giles (2004) argued that the standard error of the estimate of <i>A</i> can be used to derive that of the estimate of <i>G</i> directly without using a jackknife at all. This method only requires the use of ordinary least squares regression after ordering the sample data. The results compare favorably with the estimates from the jackknife with agreement improving with increasing sample size.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiles2004_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiles2004-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However it has since been argued that this is dependent on the model\'s assumptions about the error distributions (Ogwang 2004) and the independence of error terms (Reza &amp; Gastwirth 2006) and that these assumptions are often not valid for real data sets. It may therefore be better to stick with jackknife methods such as those proposed by <a href="/wiki/Shlomo_Yitzhaki_(economics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shlomo Yitzhaki (economics)">Yitzhaki</a> (1991) and Karagiannis and Kovacevic (2000). The debate continues.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Guillermina Jasso<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Angus_Deaton" title="Angus Deaton">Angus Deaton</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaton1997139_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaton1997139-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> independently proposed the following formula for the Gini coefficient:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle G={\\frac {N+1}{N-1}}-{\\frac {2}{N(N-1)\\mu }}(\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}\\;P_{i}X_{i})}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>G</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>N</mi>\n              <mo>+</mo>\n              <mn>1</mn>\n            </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>N</mi>\n              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n              <mn>1</mn>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mn>2</mn>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>N</mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n              <mi>N</mi>\n              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \xe2\x88\x92 --></mo>\n              <mn>1</mn>\n              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n              <mi>&#x03BC;<!-- \xce\xbc --></mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msubsup>\n          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x03A3;<!-- \xce\xa3 --></mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n            <mo>=</mo>\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>n</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msubsup>\n        <mspace width="thickmathspace" />\n        <msub>\n          <mi>P</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>X</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle G={\\frac {N+1}{N-1}}-{\\frac {2}{N(N-1)\\mu }}(\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}\\;P_{i}X_{i})}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/184df114d88979c2b9075b1bced85caa675cad0e" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:38.894ex; height:6.009ex;" alt="G={\\frac {N+1}{N-1}}-{\\frac {2}{N(N-1)\\mu }}(\\Sigma _{i=1}^{n}\\;P_{i}X_{i})"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mu }">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>&#x03BC;<!-- \xce\xbc --></mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mu }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9fd47b2a39f7a7856952afec1f1db72c67af6161" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:1.402ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\\mu "/></span> is mean income of the population, P<sub>i</sub> is the income rank P of person i, with income X, such that the richest person receives a rank of 1 and the poorest a rank of N. This effectively gives higher weight to poorer people in the income distribution, which allows the Gini to meet the <a href="/wiki/Income_inequality_metrics#Transfer_principle" title="Income inequality metrics">Transfer Principle</a>. Note that the Jasso-Deaton formula rescales the coefficient so that its value is 1 if all the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle X_{i}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>X</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle X_{i}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af4a0955af42beb5f85aa05fb8c07abedc13990d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.724ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="X_{i}"/></span> are zero except one. Note however Allison\'s reply on the need to divide by N\xc2\xb2 instead.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>FAO explains another version of the formula.<sup id="cite_ref-faogini_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faogini-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Generalized_inequality_indices">Generalized inequality indices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Generalized inequality indices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Generalized_entropy_index" title="Generalized entropy index">Generalized entropy index</a></div>\n<p>The Gini coefficient and other standard inequality indices reduce to a common form. Perfect equality\xe2\x80\x94the absence of inequality\xe2\x80\x94exists when and only when the inequality ratio, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle r_{j}=x_{j}/{\\overline {x}}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>r</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>x</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mover>\n            <mi>x</mi>\n            <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- \xc2\xaf --></mo>\n          </mover>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r_{j}=x_{j}/{\\overline {x}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e15efedea663fe578e737f2fb0c3eb317b41406a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:9.903ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="r_{j}=x_{j}/{\\overline {x}}"/></span>, equals 1 for all j units in some population (for example, there is perfect income equality when everyone\'s income <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle x_{j}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>x</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle x_{j}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5db47cb3d2f9496205a17a6856c91c1d3d363ccd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.239ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="x_{j}"/></span> equals the mean income <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\overline {x}}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mover>\n            <mi>x</mi>\n            <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- \xc2\xaf --></mo>\n          </mover>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\overline {x}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9fa4039bbc2a0048c3a3c02e5fd24390cab0dc97" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.445ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="{\\overline {x}}"/></span>, so that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle r_{j}=1}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>r</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mn>1</mn>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r_{j}=1}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d5bc0eea3ed03dd8f661949f0f2ad2ee7f5c4fed" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:6.219ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="r_{j}=1"/></span> for everyone). Measures of inequality, then, are measures of the average deviations of the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle r_{j}=1}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>r</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mn>1</mn>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r_{j}=1}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d5bc0eea3ed03dd8f661949f0f2ad2ee7f5c4fed" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:6.219ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="r_{j}=1"/></span> from 1; the greater the average deviation, the greater the inequality. Based on these observations the inequality indices have this common form:<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\text{Inequality}}=\\Sigma _{j}\\,p_{j}\\,f(r_{j})\\,,}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mtext>Inequality</mtext>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x03A3;<!-- \xce\xa3 --></mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />\n        <msub>\n          <mi>p</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />\n        <mi>f</mi>\n        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>r</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mi>j</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\text{Inequality}}=\\Sigma _{j}\\,p_{j}\\,f(r_{j})\\,,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c43e9d2f42d096f631f44e54d802785a4bc2a891" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:24.893ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="{\\text{Inequality}}=\\Sigma _{j}\\,p_{j}\\,f(r_{j})\\,,"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <i>p</i><sub><i>j</i></sub> weights the units by their population share, and <i>f</i>(<i>r</i><sub><i>j</i></sub>) is a function of the deviation of each unit\'s <i>r</i><sub><i>j</i></sub> from 1, the point of equality. The insight of this generalised inequality index is that inequality indices differ because they employ different functions of the distance of the inequality ratios (the <i>r</i><sub><i>j</i></sub>) from 1.<i></i>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gini_coefficients_of_income_distributions">Gini coefficients of income distributions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Gini coefficients of income distributions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">List of countries by income equality</a></div>\n<p>Gini coefficients of income are calculated on market income as well as disposable income basis. The Gini coefficient on market income\xe2\x80\x94sometimes referred to as a pre-tax Gini coefficient\xe2\x80\x94is calculated on income before taxes and transfers, and it measures inequality in income without considering the effect of taxes and social spending already in place in a country. The Gini coefficient on disposable income\xe2\x80\x94sometimes referred to as after-tax Gini coefficient\xe2\x80\x94is calculated on income after taxes and transfers, and it measures inequality in income after considering the effect of taxes and social spending already in place in a country.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-imf2000_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2000-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The difference in Gini indices between <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> countries, on after-taxes and transfers basis, is significantly narrower.<sup id="cite_ref-imf2000_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2000-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> For OECD countries, over 2008\xe2\x80\x932009 period, Gini coefficient on pre-taxes and transfers basis for total population ranged between 0.34 and 0.53, with South Korea the lowest and Italy the highest. Gini coefficient on after-taxes and transfers basis for total population ranged between 0.25 and 0.48, with Denmark the lowest and Mexico the highest. For United States, the country with the largest population in OECD countries, the pre-tax Gini index was 0.49, and after-tax Gini index was 0.38, in 2008\xe2\x80\x932009. The OECD averages for total population in OECD countries was 0.46 for pre-tax income Gini index and 0.31 for after-tax income Gini Index.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Taxes and social spending that were in place in 2008\xe2\x80\x932009 period in OECD countries significantly lowered effective income inequality, and in general, "European countries\xe2\x80\x94especially Nordic and Continental <a href="/wiki/Welfare_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Welfare states">welfare states</a>\xe2\x80\x94achieve lower levels of income inequality than other countries."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Using the Gini can help quantify differences in <a href="/wiki/Social_welfare" class="mw-redirect" title="Social welfare">welfare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Living_wage" title="Living wage">compensation</a> policies and philosophies. However it should be borne in mind that the Gini coefficient can be misleading when used to make political comparisons between large and small countries or those with different immigration policies (see <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient#Limitations_of_Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">limitations of Gini coefficient</a> section).\n</p><p>The Gini coefficient for the entire world has been estimated by various parties to be between 0.61 and 0.68.<sup id="cite_ref-fao2009_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-undp10_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undp10-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The graph shows the values expressed as a percentage in their historical development for a number of countries.\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:722px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gini_since_WWII.svg" class="image"><img alt="The change in Gini indices has differed across countries. Some countries have change little over time, such as Belgium, Canada, Germany, Japan, and Sweden. Brazil has oscillated around a steady value. France, Italy, Mexico, and Norway have shown marked declines. China and the US have increased steadily. Australia grew to moderate levels before dropping. India sank before rising again. The UK and Poland stayed at very low levels before rising. Bulgaria had an increase of fits-and-starts. .svg alt text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Gini_since_WWII.svg/720px-Gini_since_WWII.svg.png" width="720" height="521" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Gini_since_WWII.svg/1080px-Gini_since_WWII.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Gini_since_WWII.svg/1440px-Gini_since_WWII.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1376" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gini_since_WWII.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_income_Gini_indices">Regional income Gini indices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Regional income Gini indices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to UNICEF, Latin America and the Caribbean region had the highest net income Gini index in the world at 48.3, on unweighted average basis in 2008. The remaining regional averages were: sub-Saharan Africa (44.2), Asia (40.4), Middle East and North Africa (39.2), Eastern Europe and Central Asia (35.4), and High-income Countries (30.9). Using the same method, the United States is claimed to have a Gini index of 36, while South Africa had the highest income Gini index score of 67.8.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef2011_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef2011-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_income_Gini_index_since_1800s">World income Gini index since 1800s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: World income Gini index since 1800s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif/310px-Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif" width="310" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif/465px-Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif/620px-Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif 2x" data-file-width="978" data-file-height="528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berg_Ostry_2011_Chart_4.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Growth spells last longer in more equal countries. A 10 percentile increase in equality (represented by a change in the Gini index value from 40 to 37) increases the expected length of a growth spell by 50 percent. Percentage changes in GDP growth spell length are shown as each factor moves from 50th to 60th percentile and all other factors are held constant. <b>Income distribution is measured by the Gini coefficient.</b><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The table below presents the estimated world income Gini coefficients over the last 200 years, as calculated by Milanovic.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Taking income distribution of all human beings, the worldwide income inequality has been constantly increasing since the early 19th century. There was a steady increase in the global income inequality Gini score from 1820 to 2002, with a significant increase between 1980 and 2002. This trend appears to have peaked and begun a reversal with rapid economic growth in emerging economies, particularly in the large populations of <a href="/wiki/BRIC" title="BRIC">BRIC</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n<caption>Income Gini coefficient<br />World, 1820\xe2\x80\x932005\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>World Gini coefficients<sup id="cite_ref-fao2009_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unicef2011_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef2011-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1820</td>\n<td>0.43\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1850</td>\n<td>0.53\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1870</td>\n<td>0.56\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1913</td>\n<td>0.61\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1929</td>\n<td>0.62\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1950</td>\n<td>0.64\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1960</td>\n<td>0.64\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1980</td>\n<td>0.66\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2002</td>\n<td>0.71\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2005</td>\n<td>0.68\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>More detailed data from similar sources plots a continuous decline since 1988.  This is attributed to <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> increasing incomes for billions of poor people, mostly in India and China.  Developing countries like Brazil have also improved basic services like health care, education, and sanitation; others like Chile and Mexico have enacted more <a href="/wiki/Progressive_tax" title="Progressive tax">progressive tax</a> policies.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year\n</th>\n<th>World Gini coefficient<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1988\n</td>\n<td>.80\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1993\n</td>\n<td>.76\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1998\n</td>\n<td>.74\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2003\n</td>\n<td>.72\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2008\n</td>\n<td>.70\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2013\n</td>\n<td>.65\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gini_coefficients_of_social_development">Gini coefficients of social development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Gini coefficients of social development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Gini coefficient is widely used in fields as diverse as sociology, economics, health science, ecology, engineering and agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-Sadras_2004_303\xe2\x80\x93310_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sadras_2004_303\xe2\x80\x93310-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> For example, in social sciences and economics, in addition to income Gini coefficients, scholars have published education Gini coefficients and opportunity Gini coefficients.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gini_coefficient_of_education">Gini coefficient of education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Gini coefficient of education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Education Gini index estimates the inequality in education for a given population.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> It is used to discern trends in social development through educational attainment over time. From a study of 85 countries by three Economists of World Bank Vinod Thomas, Yan Wang, Xibo Fan, estimate Mali had the highest education Gini index of 0.92 in 1990 (implying very high inequality in education attainment across the population), while the United States had the lowest education inequality Gini index of 0.14. Between 1960 and 1990, South Korea, China and India had the fastest drop in education inequality Gini Index. They also claim education Gini index for the United States slightly increased over the 1980\xe2\x80\x931990 period.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gini_coefficient_of_opportunity">Gini coefficient of opportunity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Gini coefficient of opportunity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Similar in concept to income Gini coefficient, opportunity Gini coefficient measures inequality of opportunity.<sup id="cite_ref-roemer06_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roemer06-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The concept builds on <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>\'s suggestion<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> that inequality coefficients of social development should be premised on the process of enlarging people\'s choices and enhancing their capabilities, rather than on the process of reducing income inequality. Kovacevic in a review of opportunity Gini coefficient explains that the coefficient estimates how well a society enables its citizens to achieve success in life where the success is based on a person\'s choices, efforts and talents, not his background defined by a set of predetermined circumstances at birth, such as, gender, race, place of birth, parent\'s income and circumstances beyond the control of that individual.\n</p><p>In 2003, Roemer<sup id="cite_ref-roemer06_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roemer06-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> reported Italy and Spain exhibited the largest opportunity inequality Gini index amongst advanced economies.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gini_coefficients_and_income_mobility">Gini coefficients and income mobility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Gini coefficients and income mobility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1978, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Shorrocks" title="Anthony Shorrocks">Anthony Shorrocks</a> introduced a measure based on income Gini coefficients to estimate income mobility.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> This measure, generalized by Maasoumi and Zandvakili,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> is now generally referred to as <a href="/wiki/Shorrocks_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Shorrocks index">Shorrocks index</a>, sometimes as Shorrocks mobility index or Shorrocks rigidity index. It attempts to estimate whether the income inequality Gini coefficient is permanent or temporary, and to what extent a country or region enables economic mobility to its people so that they can move from one (e.g. bottom 20%) income quantile to another (e.g. middle 20%) over time. In other words, Shorrocks index compares inequality of short-term earnings such as annual income of households, to inequality of long-term earnings such as 5-year or 10-year total income for same households.\n</p><p>Shorrocks index is calculated in number of different ways, a common approach being from the ratio of income Gini coefficients between short-term and long-term for the same region or country.<sup id="cite_ref-kss2010_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kss2010-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 2010 study using social security income data for the United States since 1937 and Gini-based Shorrocks indices concludes that income mobility in the United States has had a complicated history, primarily due to mass influx of women into the American labor force after World War II. Income inequality and income mobility trendsc have been different for men and women workers between 1937 and the 2000s. When men and women are considered together, the Gini coefficient-based Shorrocks index trends imply long-term income inequality has been substantially reduced among all workers, in recent decades for the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-kss2010_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kss2010-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Other scholars, using just 1990s data or other short periods have come to different conclusions.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> For example, Sastre and Ayala, conclude from their study of income Gini coefficient data between 1993 and 1998 for six developed economies, that France had the least income mobility, Italy the highest, and the United States and Germany intermediate levels of income mobility over those 5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features_of_Gini_coefficient">Features of Gini coefficient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gini_coefficient&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Features of Gini coefficient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Gini coefficient has features that make it useful as a measure of dispersion in a population, and inequalities in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-faogini_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faogini-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Ratio_analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ratio analysis">ratio analysis</a> method making it easier to interpret. It also avoids references to a statistical average or position unrepresentative of most of the population, such as <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> or <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>. For a given time interval, Gini coefficient can therefore be used to compare diverse countries and different regions or groups within a country; for example states, counties, urban versus rural areas, gender and ethnic groups.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Gini coefficients can be used to compare income distribution over time, thus it is possible to see if inequality is increasing or decreasing independent of absolute incomes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Other useful features of the Gini coefficient include:<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Need RS (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Development_Economics,_Debraj_Ray_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Development_Economics,_Debraj_Ray-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Anonymity</i>: it does not matter who the high and low earners are.</li>\n<li><i>Scale independence</i>: the Gini coefficient does not consider the size of the economy, the way it is measured, or whether it is a rich or poor country on average.</li>\n<li><i>Population independence</i>: it does not matter how large the population of the country is.</li>\n<li><i>Transfer principle</i>: if income (less than the difference), is transferred from a rich person to a poor person the resulting distribution is more equal.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_by_Gini_Index">Countries by Gini Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
